<div id="review_46671146" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46671146" />
    <a title="Darbus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1278644-darbus"><img alt="Darbus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226722100p2/1278644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46671146?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darbus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darbus" href="/user/show/1278644-darbus">Darbus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1278644-darbus?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer46671146&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46671146" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer82773307973636689">Before I begin, allow me to puke in a corner. Now that I'm done with that, here's what I thought. It wasn't all it was cracked up to be, that's for sure. I have a lengthy list of complaints. To begin with, there were countless grammatical errors. Honestly, Bujold, it's possible to use more than one comma in a sentence, get verb tenses correct, and use pronouns to increase clarity. I'm not going to give it one star, just based on the fact that there are books that are a lot worse. <br/><br/>The characters/</span>
  <span id="freeText82773307973636689" style="display:none">Before I begin, allow me to puke in a corner. Now that I'm done with that, here's what I thought. It wasn't all it was cracked up to be, that's for sure. I have a lengthy list of complaints. To begin with, there were countless grammatical errors. Honestly, Bujold, it's possible to use more than one comma in a sentence, get verb tenses correct, and use pronouns to increase clarity. I'm not going to give it one star, just based on the fact that there are books that are a lot worse. <br /><br />The characters/their development were another huge problem. For one, Cordelia completely changed personalities. She was a straightforward, determined, focused, responsible military woman at the beginning of Shards of Honor. By the end of just that half of it, she had transformed into a whiny and annoying typical female 'heroine.' I believe that her last action that I completely agreed with was trying to drown that shrink. After that, all her thoughts were were about her baby, playing matchmaker for Kou and Drou, or about how Beta Colony was <i>so much</i> better than Barrayar. She regained a bit of her former personality during their rait, but immediately lost it when dealing with the birth, or with Kou/Drou. Also, her love for Vorkosigan wasn't very well explained. Other characters only had one major characteristic, and that was frequently variable. Count Piotr is a good example of that. <br /><br />The plot of Barrayar was fairly lame. It was all about Cordelia's whining about being pregnant or whining about how primitive Barrayar was, and it kept picking up and then suddenly dropping sub-plots. </span>
  <a data-text-id="82773307973636689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1107171-libby?shelf=year-of-women">year-of-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1107171-libby?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153448084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3608906643273422700">I very much enjoyed these early books in the Vorkosigan saga, despite the fact that there are plenty of new-author moments that occasionally jarred me from the narrative. These human civilizations feel very much designed to showcase the characters rather than showcase the author's world-building. Fortunately, this works very well for these books because the main characters, the titular surveyor-turned-soldier from Beta Colony, Cordelia, and Barrayan soldier-lord Aral Vorkosigan, are utterly enga</span>
  <span id="freeText3608906643273422700" style="display:none">I very much enjoyed these early books in the Vorkosigan saga, despite the fact that there are plenty of new-author moments that occasionally jarred me from the narrative. These human civilizations feel very much designed to showcase the characters rather than showcase the author's world-building. Fortunately, this works very well for these books because the main characters, the titular surveyor-turned-soldier from Beta Colony, Cordelia, and Barrayan soldier-lord Aral Vorkosigan, are utterly engaging, and the supporting cast is equally strong. Also excellent are Bujold's action sequences, which are invariably well-paced and clear.<br /><br />Where the books occasionally fall flat are when the plot is taken hostage by the need to prove a capital-p Point. For instance, <br /><br />SPOILER<br /><br />the climactic scene in "Barrayar" where Cordelia and company break into the imperial palace, presumably to rescue hostages, and they come up in the bedroom of the usurper, who is asleep with the princess dowager. Instead of using her borrowed swordstick to slit the traitor's throat, Cordelia muses that her electronic weapon would set off alarms if she uses it to kill him. The purpose of this more than slight oversight is so the princess dowager can be shown to be a victim rather than an active participant. After an annoyingly manipulative scene involving her son's shoe, the princess is killed in crossfire, thus becoming a symbol of the capital-t Theme: patriarchal society harms women irreparably. <br /><br />END SPOILER<br /><br />All in all, I'd recommend these books for any sci-fi fan who hasn't already read them, and they're thus far wholly appropriate for a YA audience. I am very much looking forward to reading more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3608906643273422700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15226736369088294652">Lois has written one of the best love stories in the little-known subgenre of Romance SF with this duology. Two halves of one book, IMO, this story anchors the entire series for the next 20 years of Lois's writing, Miles's life, and the universe's existence. Except at the center of this universe is Aral Vorkosigan and it is ONLY in this book (pair of books) that we really and truly get to know Aral's heart. Which is, of course, named Cordelia ;-) The Admiral's Captain, Cordelia Naismith and Admi</span>
  <span id="freeText15226736369088294652" style="display:none">Lois has written one of the best love stories in the little-known subgenre of Romance SF with this duology. Two halves of one book, IMO, this story anchors the entire series for the next 20 years of Lois's writing, Miles's life, and the universe's existence. Except at the center of this universe is Aral Vorkosigan and it is ONLY in this book (pair of books) that we really and truly get to know Aral's heart. Which is, of course, named Cordelia ;-) The Admiral's Captain, Cordelia Naismith and Admiral Count Aral Vorkosigan, The Butcher of Komarr have quite the little love affair that wasn't. The way the man courts without courting--not to mention the way this woman flirts without batting an eyelash. Well, maybe while she was retching on his boots her eyelashes batted a bit but after that, she kept both eyes open and on the Enemy :) Great story, great love affair, great masterpiece of art created by a very humble Lady Bujold.</span>

<div id="review_27842103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27842103" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/296169-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1192646270p2/296169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27842103?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/296169-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/296169-anne?shelf=read2008">read2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/296169-anne?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/296169-anne?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer27842103&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27842103" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer867604466159932116">I first read this book about 8 years ago, and it remains one of my all time favorites.<br/><br/><i>Cordelia's Honor</i> is actually a compilation of two of Lois McMaster Bujold's earlier books, <i>Shards of Honor</i> and <i>Barrayar</i>. It is part of the Vorkosigan saga, but I had not read any of the others when I first read this one. The book is told from the point of view of Cordelia Naismith, Captain of a Betan Survey ship. While on survey, her crew is attacked by a band of Barrayans, led by none other than Aral Vorkosiga</span>
  <span id="freeText867604466159932116" style="display:none">I first read this book about 8 years ago, and it remains one of my all time favorites.<br /><br /><i>Cordelia's Honor</i> is actually a compilation of two of Lois McMaster Bujold's earlier books, <i>Shards of Honor</i> and <i>Barrayar</i>. It is part of the Vorkosigan saga, but I had not read any of the others when I first read this one. The book is told from the point of view of Cordelia Naismith, Captain of a Betan Survey ship. While on survey, her crew is attacked by a band of Barrayans, led by none other than Aral Vorkosigan, aka The Butcher of Komarr.<br /><br />In truth, Vorkosigan, is actually the victim of a conspiracy to kill him and frame him for the attack on the Betans. As Cordelia travels with him to safety, she gets to know and admire him. Both of them are military people for whom responsibility means everything. Unfortunately, they’re on opposite sides of a brewing war.<br /><br />Romance and science fiction rarely blend smoothly. You either end up with the same old romance story just set in outer space, or a science fiction story with really bad romantic scenes. Cordelia’s Honor is the exception; it is the perfect harmony of both.<br /><br />What makes this book so successful is the characterization. I read a lot, but Bujold has written some of the most engaging, realistic characters I’ve read in a long time. Especially Cordelia. I loved Cordelia, I want to <b>be</b> Cordelia. She’s witty, strong, smart and, well for lack of a better term, a kick butt heroine. She is not content to huddle quietly and wait for her man to rescue her from the bad guys. Nope; she gets up and blasts them with her stunner without so much as a by your leave. This is not to say she’s one of those annoyingly all men are idiots types either. She’s attracted to Vorkosigan, not afraid to admit it and rather likes the idea. Even better, Cordelia is not a young, sexy spacebunny in a tight suit. She’s in her 30’s, a little on the tall side and just a regular looking woman. Did I mention I loved her?<br /><br />As easy as it is to see why Vorkosigan would fall for Cordelia, it’s just as easy to see why she falls for him. No studmuffin himself, Vorkosigan is in his 40’s and just barely taller than Cordelia (which makes him short for a man) Though on the outside he’s all business, inside he’s a honorable man who is reluctantly dragged into the political messes of his world. He finds he can open up to Cordelia, and does so with refreshing ease. Too many SF heroes (and romance heroes for that matter) are of the breed that would rather get a root canal than express their emotions or communicate. He’s also a great foil for Cordelia’s dry wit, giving as good as he gets.<br /><br />Bujold doesn’t stop at the main characters either. The small cast of secondary characters, such as the mentally interesting Sergeant Bothari, is three dimensional and as intriguing as the main characters. You care about all of them, no matter how small their actual part in the story.<br /><br />The first half of the book, (Shards of Honor) covers the developing relationship between Cordelia and Vorkosgian through their trek on the survey planet and the Betan/Barrayan war. The second half (Barrayar) starts shortly after their wedding and covers Cordelia’s acclimation to life as Lady Vorkosgian and the political wrangling after Aral is named Regent for the child emperor. I found this part of the book dragged in places. I would have preferred less political intrigue and more Cordelia/Vorkosigan, but still <i>Barrayar</i> is one of the best of the genre (and it won the Hugo award for best novel).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="867604466159932116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_240502279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240502279" />
    <a title="D. Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4251292-d-jason"><img alt="D. Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442888988p2/4251292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240502279?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="D. Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="D. Jason" href="/user/show/4251292-d-jason">D. Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=epub-editions">epub-editions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=baen-books">baen-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4251292-d-jason?shelf=vorkosigan-series">vorkosigan-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240502279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer693598845759579318">This is a collection of two novels which tell a single story, Shards Of Honor and Barrayar. <br/><br/>Shards Of Honor is Bujold's first book and, judged in that light, it's very, very good. Judged against the rest of the Vorkosigan series, however, it comes off less well. The ingredients are there, physical adventure and well-thought out characters bouncing off each other, but they don't jell the way they do even in Bujold's second book, The Warrior's Apprentice (in the Young Miles omnibus).<br/><br/>Cordelia Naism</span>
  <span id="freeText693598845759579318" style="display:none">This is a collection of two novels which tell a single story, Shards Of Honor and Barrayar. <br /><br />Shards Of Honor is Bujold's first book and, judged in that light, it's very, very good. Judged against the rest of the Vorkosigan series, however, it comes off less well. The ingredients are there, physical adventure and well-thought out characters bouncing off each other, but they don't jell the way they do even in Bujold's second book, The Warrior's Apprentice (in the Young Miles omnibus).<br /><br />Cordelia Naismith is the captain of a scientific survey mission from Beta Colony, studying a planet discovered in a new node in the wormhole nexus (Bujold's wonderfully 1980s means of bypassing the speed of light). Very quickly, she finds her crew slaughtered and herself prisoner of a soldier from Barrayar, a militarist, feudal planet that was isolated from galactic civilization for hundreds of years, only rejoined in the past century or so. And not just any soldier, either. Admiral Aral Vorkosigan, the Butcher of Komarr. At first she fears him due to his reputation. But as they are thrown together, more or less alone (he's been betrayed by some of his soldiers, and the rest believe him dead), she comes to judge him as a good, even noble, man -- in spite of his own judgement that his reputation is at least somewhat deserved.<br /><br />(An aside: The single most unbelievable aspect of the book, to me, is the notion that Cordelia views herself as unattractive. She is tall, red-headed, and her features are described at least once as "handsome" by another, I believe. Also, she's a scientist and a leader of men, strong in character. Clearly, this is some strange new definition of "unattractive" of which I was previously unaware.)<br /><br />For some reason I've never been able to identify, I always enjoy Shards Of Honor a great deal while reading it, and then the enjoyment fades sharply after I finish it. So it's three, maybe four stars if I'm being generous.<br /><br />Barrayar, on the other hand, needs no generosity. It kicks unholy ass. :)<br /><br />Continuing Cordelia's story almost immediately after Shards (it picks up a day or two after the closing scenes of the earlier book), but written more than a half-dozen books (and two Hugos and two Nebulas) later, Bujold's firing on all cylinders in this one. <br /><br />Aral and Cordelia are married, Cordelia's newly pregnant, and Aral is Regent of the Barrayaran Empire (for complicated reasons demonstrated in the earlier book). However, there are forces in Barrayaran society that do not appreciate the path events are taking, and they blame the Regent. Before the book is half over, a violent coup is in progress, and Cordelia and Aral are on the run again, this time separately -- Aral must plot a counterstrike, while Cordelia tries to keep the five year old Emperor hidden and alive.<br /><br />It's brilliant, completely entertaining, exciting, and only gets better on rereading. Five stars. It's so good that I'm giving the whole omnibus five stars, rather than averaging the scores together.<br /><br />(I was purposely vague, even refraining from spoiling things that would not have been considered spoilers to fans of the series when the book came out. I'm funny that way.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="693598845759579318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_131800065" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131800065" />
    <a title="Misha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/175912-misha"><img alt="Misha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599365681p2/175912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131800065?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misha" href="/user/show/175912-misha">Misha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175912-misha?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175912-misha?shelf=motherhood">motherhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175912-misha?shelf=love-story">love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175912-misha?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131800065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18355780064074468799">Cordelia is on a planetary expedition when she is taken captive by Lord Vorkosigan. Their unexpected romance brings her to planet Barrayar where politics prove seriously life-threatening to them and their unborn son.<br/><br/>I have long heard that Bujold’s Vorkosigan series was a good series. I knew she wrote “military sf,” which never sounded good to me. But I thought that I should give Bujold a try; so many patrons and friends have mentioned her in glowing terms over the years. In creating a recent Fan</span>
  <span id="freeText18355780064074468799" style="display:none">Cordelia is on a planetary expedition when she is taken captive by Lord Vorkosigan. Their unexpected romance brings her to planet Barrayar where politics prove seriously life-threatening to them and their unborn son.<br /><br />I have long heard that Bujold’s Vorkosigan series was a good series. I knew she wrote “military sf,” which never sounded good to me. But I thought that I should give Bujold a try; so many patrons and friends have mentioned her in glowing terms over the years. In creating a recent Fantasy list, I also discovered that she writes fantasy as well.<br /><br />Cordelia’s Honor is comprised of two books: Shards of Honor and Barrayar. There is more romance in these novels than I originally expected and more sexual violence as well. But there is some really interesting politics and world building. Cordelia is a Betan; Beta Colony is a world where poverty has been eradicated, you must apply to the government to become parents, women are implanted with contraceptive chips and babies can be placed in uterine replicators. Vorkosigan’s Barrayar is a military-obsessed planet that is more physically beautiful but offers less equality and technological advances for its people and women are still not on equal footing with men. There is a lot of action from the get-go. <br /><br />Here are a couple of passages that struck me.<br />Cordelia, on children: “Save me from that! To pour your life into sons for eighteen or twenty years, and then have the government take them away and waste them cleaning up after some failure of politics—no thanks.” (41)<br />Vorkosigan: “The real unforgiveable acts are committed by calm men in beautiful green silk rooms, who deal death wholesale, by the shipload, without lust, or anger, or desire, or any redeeming emotion to excuse them but cold fear of some pretended future. But the crimes they hope to prevent in that future are imaginary. The ones they commit in the present—they are real.” (141)<br /><br />For one, this is a love story and a story about motherhood. But both Cordelia and Aral contradict the proclamations above; in a way, it reminded me of a phrase my best friend and I used to write in our high school letters: “My contradictions are my hopes.” Cordelia and Aral cannot seem to choose a quiet life; even in their love from one another, they cannot help but choose the more difficult path. Aral becomes the Regent, a stand-in ruler until the Prince comes of age, but an assassination attempt and a military coup leave Aral and Cordelia in the hospital, their child’s life in jeopardy, and, ultimately has them on the run and on the defensive. I was overall impressed with the scope and characterization and I think that I may have to read Young Miles at some point, too.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18355780064074468799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_318615392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318615392" />
    <a title="Jared Millet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1032237-jared-millet"><img alt="Jared Millet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566869109p2/1032237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318615392?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jared Millet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jared Millet" href="/user/show/1032237-jared-millet">Jared Millet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1032237-jared-millet?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1032237-jared-millet?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1032237-jared-millet?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1032237-jared-millet?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318615392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10415587585912861248"><b>
  <i>Shards of Honor</i>
</b><br/><br/>The first of the Vorkosigan books surprised me by being more of a romance novel than I was expecting, but I don't begrudge it. It was actually refreshing to read a romance plot that didn't fall into the overused "Pride and Prejudice" formula. Bujold doesn't waste any time trying to make us think her heroine despises the hero, and he doesn't waste the whole novel bending heaven and earth to impress her. They both have their own lives and their own problems - namely that they're</span>
  <span id="freeText10415587585912861248" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Shards of Honor</i>
</b><br /><br />The first of the Vorkosigan books surprised me by being more of a romance novel than I was expecting, but I don't begrudge it. It was actually refreshing to read a romance plot that didn't fall into the overused "Pride and Prejudice" formula. Bujold doesn't waste any time trying to make us think her heroine despises the hero, and he doesn't waste the whole novel bending heaven and earth to impress her. They both have their own lives and their own problems - namely that they're military officers from enemy planets. <i>And yet</i> the novel doesn't fall into the Romeo &amp; Juliet formula either. Instead, you get two characters who are attracted to each other, know it, and want to be together, but duty to their respective cultures keep them apart until both of the homeworlds they cherish turn against them in one way or another.<br /><br />It probably sounds like I'm spoiling the book, but I'm really not. The problem was that almost nothing in the novel came as a surprise aside from a few shocking coincidences and points of political intrigue. But the characters were so engaging (and Bujold so successful in making me care about them) that a predictable storyline can be forgiven.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Barrayar</i>
</b><br /><br />Now this one I'm on the fence about, which is odd since it won the Hugo. (I just checked the slate for that year and WTF - it beat <i>Stations of the Tide</i>? Uh, no - I don't think so.) <br /><br />As a novel it works better than <i>Shards</i>: the plot is more coherent, the characters are better drawn, their motivations are more consistent. I think my problem was that it wasn't science-fictional enough. <i>Shards</i> had space battles, a futuristic society, and settings on two non-earthlike planets. The world of Barrayar, on the other hand, is just 18th century Prussia with ray guns and flying cars. Furthermore, the political intrigue this time around just wasn't intriguing. In <i>Shards</i>, the Barrayaran emperor's final plot was wonderfully Byzantine and Machiavellian. <i>Barrayar</i>, on the other hand, has nothing but a run-of-the-mill attempted coup with antagonists who are neither complex nor particularly competent.<br /><br />Two things save it: 1) Cordelia's main concern isn't for winning the war, but for protecting her unborn son. To her, the war is only secondary. 2) Piotr Vorkosigan, Cordelia's father-in-law, the only character with shades of gray. Everyone in the book is clearly on one side of the conflict or the other, but Piotr - while loyal to the "good guys" - is also a danger to Cordelia.<br /><br />Anyhow, the books are both well-written and I'm told that if I enjoyed these even a little I should love the Miles Vorkosigan books that come after.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10415587585912861248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_101241781" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101241781" />
    <a title="Hazel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2253648-hazel"><img alt="Hazel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101241781?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hazel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hazel" href="/user/show/2253648-hazel">Hazel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2253648-hazel?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2253648-hazel?shelf=non-genre-romantic-story">non-genre-romantic-story</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101241781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4115411267809602860">Just arrived. Thank you, Amazon! I've read each of the novels years ago, probably more than once, and was reminded of them by a recent review. Cordelia and Aral are a good example of an adult couple. Theirs is a grown up romance, as one of my friends said. Here's my favourite quote from <i>Shards of Honour</i>.<br/><br/><blockquote>They crossed another watercourse. Coming up over the lip of its valley, Cordelia nearly stumbled over a red-coated hexaped, lying quite still in a depression and blending perfectly with its backg</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4115411267809602860" style="display:none">Just arrived. Thank you, Amazon! I've read each of the novels years ago, probably more than once, and was reminded of them by a recent review. Cordelia and Aral are a good example of an adult couple. Theirs is a grown up romance, as one of my friends said. Here's my favourite quote from <i>Shards of Honour</i>.<br /><br /><blockquote>They crossed another watercourse. Coming up over the lip of its valley, Cordelia nearly stumbled over a red-coated hexaped, lying quite still in a depression and blending perfectly with its background. It was a delicately formed thing, as big as a middle-sized dog, and it rippled over the red plains in graceful bounds.<br /> Cordelia woke up abruptly. "That thing's edible!"<br /> "The stunner, the stunner!" cried Vorkosigan. She pressed it hastily into his hand. He fell to one knee, took aim, and dropped the creature in one burst.<br /> "Oh, good shot!" cried Cordelia ecstatically.<br /> Vorkosigan grinned like a boy over his shoulder at her, and jogged after his prize.<br /> "Oh," she murmured, stunned herself by the effect of the grin. It had lit his face like the sun for that brief instant. Oh, do that again, she thought; then shook off the thought. Duty. Stick to duty.</blockquote><br /><br />Don't be fooled though. This is proper science fiction, and a proper adventure story. There is exploration and espionage, and covert-ops; there is war, and there are war crimes. There are medical and social advances and ethical dilemmas. And there are timeless stories of family conflicts, loyalty and friendship. (And love.) I didn't recognise the complexity of <i>Barrayar</i> the first time I read it. But it strikes me now that I understand why it won the Hugo that year.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4115411267809602860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_358234451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358234451" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2061204-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358234451?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/2061204-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2061204-christy?shelf=1-own-it-book">1-own-it-book</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358234451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11915559306779617390">5 stars for the omnibus edition, because these books really belong together, and because of her insightful afterword. I can tell this will be a volume I re-read multiple times. <br/><br/>4 stars for Shards of Honor<br/>Cordelia is a wonderful character, and watching her relationship with Aral develop is a real pleasure. The contrast between Barryan and Betan world-views is a major element, with the awful price of honor the major theme. My only complaints are that in telling this story, Bujold is a little too e</span>
  <span id="freeText11915559306779617390" style="display:none">5 stars for the omnibus edition, because these books really belong together, and because of her insightful afterword. I can tell this will be a volume I re-read multiple times. <br /><br />4 stars for Shards of Honor<br />Cordelia is a wonderful character, and watching her relationship with Aral develop is a real pleasure. The contrast between Barryan and Betan world-views is a major element, with the awful price of honor the major theme. My only complaints are that in telling this story, Bujold is a little too elliptical at times, leaving a bit too much left unsaid. But that's a minor quibble with this fascinating introduction to the Vorkosiverse. <br /><br />5 stars for Barryar<br />This is as good a sci fi novel as I'm likely to read, by which of course I mean that it hit all the right notes for me. This book includes so many elements of a great novel: a fascinating and varied cast of characters, lots of twisty intrigue, and adventure with the highest of stakes But what makes this book so emotionally searing is something that Bujold discusses in her afterword: this book explores the price of becoming a parent, particularly a mother, and does so not only for Cordelia and Aral, but with all the supporting couples providing 'symphonic variations' on the theme. I don't think you have to relate to this aspect of the book in any way to find it a terrific story (except insofar as we all have parents of one sort or another), but to me it adds a much deeper emotional resonance. If it weren't for the other eight books in the series that I haven't read yet, I'd start re-reading this right away. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11915559306779617390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_129007513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129007513" />
    <a title="Estara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3590834-estara"><img alt="Estara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271356174p2/3590834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129007513?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Estara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Estara" href="/user/show/3590834-estara">Estara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">character-driven sf who enjoy strong females</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Estara by: </span>
      auto-buy author
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer129007513&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129007513" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1882332648159261982">I'm already finished with Shards of Honor and it's a much more gritty military book on the re-read. They really de-constructed Cordelia, especially at home. I wonder how many soldiers returning from war have similar experiences. I'm reading Barrayar too, but already dreading the poisoning scene.<br/><br/>One huge advantage of this ebook edition is the afterword by LMB who mentions the main threads in the story she wrote and you really can see the thought of parents and children and what you sacrifice for </span>
  <span id="freeText1882332648159261982" style="display:none">I'm already finished with Shards of Honor and it's a much more gritty military book on the re-read. They really de-constructed Cordelia, especially at home. I wonder how many soldiers returning from war have similar experiences. I'm reading Barrayar too, but already dreading the poisoning scene.<br /><br />One huge advantage of this ebook edition is the afterword by LMB who mentions the main threads in the story she wrote and you really can see the thought of parents and children and what you sacrifice for family in Barrayar - where Aral basically has to pick up a whole empire to make sure his son will have a world worth living in, as will his Betan wife. And Cordelia has to decide to stay by his side for love and sanity and the friends she has made, as well.<br /><br />It's just heartbreaking and cathartic at the same time. Incredible work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1882332648159261982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_899768745" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/899768745" />
    <a title="Nyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2158790-nyssa"><img alt="Nyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577851535p2/2158790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/899768745?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nyssa" href="/user/show/2158790-nyssa">Nyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/10864992-cordelia-s-honor">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nyssa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3172003-jose-bueno">Jose Bueno</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=grg-flights-of-fantasy">grg-flights-of-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=format-omnibus">format-omnibus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=acc-hugo-award">acc-hugo-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=acc-locus-award">acc-locus-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158790-nyssa?shelf=series-completely-written">series-completely-written</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer899768745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10705224944751572002">Cordelia's Honor is, I believe, what the introduction to the Vorkosigan Saga was meant to be - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61903.Shards_of_Honour__Vorkosigan_Saga___1_' title='Shards of Honour (Vorkosigan Saga, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shards of Honour</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar__Vorkosigan_Saga___7_' title='Barrayar (Vorkosigan Saga, #7) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Barrayar</a> as one complete story. I can not imagine reading the two, completely separated by numerous other books and short stories, as they are when read in publication order. I am curious as to how either made sense "alone", especially with Shards of Honour being so sparse in its detail and storytelling. <br/><br/><br/></span>
  <span id="freeText10705224944751572002" style="display:none">Cordelia's Honor is, I believe, what the introduction to the Vorkosigan Saga was meant to be - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61903.Shards_of_Honour__Vorkosigan_Saga___1_" title="Shards of Honour (Vorkosigan Saga, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Shards of Honour</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar__Vorkosigan_Saga___7_" title="Barrayar (Vorkosigan Saga, #7) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Barrayar</a> as one complete story. I can not imagine reading the two, completely separated by numerous other books and short stories, as they are when read in publication order. I am curious as to how either made sense "alone", especially with Shards of Honour being so sparse in its detail and storytelling. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10705224944751572002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('W1aTrdy2qyFz7VwlW5IbuUe7UcrIQ4lM4vA7hUr8YSe2NMnd63OehM1zE2WfeGB3vdS0ZOdl12ix8GVc3bq6rQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WUAn5s9xJLEFYFLxUHMT/+HSbtSVwzzC26CZcBQgCH60In2W+LQRFLv+HbGUmWgxG72LerrlYuaIoMepg2bT9A==')})
  }

Not only did the wormhole drop him in the middle of a civil war over a depleted resource, but the battle is actually taking place inside his father’s brain. Bernard has one chance to save the dying side of his father’s creative brain from the tyrannical left side. <span id="freeTextContainer18162159537962339464">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br/><br/>Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestse</span>
  <span id="freeText18162159537962339464" style="display:none">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br /><br />Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestselling Vorkosigan Saga. Her work has been translated into over twenty languages.<br /><br />A listing of her awards and nominations may be seen here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bujold">http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bu...</a><br /> <br />A listing of her interviews is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Author_Interviews">http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Auth...</a><br /><br />An older fan-run site devoted to her work, The Bujold Nexus, is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dendarii.com/">http://www.dendarii.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
